\\u0026#34;mistral/magistral-small-latest\\u0026#34;,\\n    \\u0026#34;nvidia/minimaxai/minimax-m2.1\\u0026#34;,\\n    \\u0026#34;openrouter/nvidia/nemotron-3-super-120b-a12b:free\\u0026#34;,\\n 适配器在构造请求时，可能包含了 Mistral API 不接受的字段，例如：\\n\\n- `logit_bias`\\n- `logprobs` / `top_logprobs`\\n- `user` (OpenAI 特有)\\n- 或其他 OpenAI 特定扩展参数\\n\\nMistral API 虽然兼容 OpenAI 协议，但对参数验证更严格，某些字段会直接导致 422 临时工作around\\n\\n1. 继续使用其他 provider（如 stepfun）\\n2. 直接通过 curl/脚本调用 Mistral API\\n3. 创建自定义 skill 封装调用（已验证可行）\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 附加信息\\n\\n- OpenClaw 配置热重载正常，`mistral-small-latest` 已在 There is no configuration path to opt into private network access, even in explicitly local gateway deployments where SSRF risk is not a concern.\\n\\n### Proposed solution\\n\\nIntroduce an `allowPrivateNetwork` boolean option for `web_fetch`, `web_search`, and `image_tool`. When running in `local` gateway mode, automatically set `allowPrivateNetwork: true` for a seamless local-first experience. Wire this flag through the SSRF guard (`fetchWithSsrFGuard`) so that private addresses are reachable when the option is enabled.\\n\\n### Alternatives considered\\n\\nManually whitelisting specific IPs in the SSRF guard — too brittle and requires code changes per deployment. Routing local services through a public proxy — adds unnecessary latency and defeats the purpose of self-hosting.\\n\\n### Impact\\n\\n- **Affected:** Teams running self-hosted search engines (SearXNG, etc.) or air-gapped/private deployments\\n- **Severity:** Blocks workflow — private network access is completely unavailable today\\n- **Frequency:** Always, for any private-network roots from `getAgentScopedMediaLocalRoots`, which only includes:\\n- System temp dir\\n- `~/.openclaw/media/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/agents/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/workspace/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/sandboxes/`\\n- `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`) that correctly validates inbound attachments — but those roots are **not passed through** to the image tool's `localRoots` parameter. The two security checks are disconnected.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure iMessage channel with `includeAttachments: true`\\n2. Send an image via iMessage\\n3. Call the `image` tool with the path from the inbound message metadata\\n4. → `LocalMediaAccessError: path-not-allowed`\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\nThe iMessage channel's `attachmentRoots` should be merged into `mediaLocalRoots` when dispatching to the agent, so the `image` tool can read inbound attachments from their native Messages paths. This worked before 2026.3.2.\\n\\n## Config\\n\\n```json\\nchannels.imessage.includeAttachments: true\\n```\\nNo explicit `attachmentRoots` set (using default `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`).\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\nIn the iMessage inbound dispatch path, merge `attachmentRoots` into the `mediaLocalRoots` passed to the tool execution context — similar to how other channels handle scoped media /Users/aikoorhon/Library/Messages/Attachments/df/15/0449D7CE-A973-4444-BAD7-514214D5F00A/IMG_3719.png\\n```\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nThe `image` tool validates paths via `assertLocalMediaAllowed` using roots from `getAgentScopedMediaLocalRoots`, which only includes:\\n- System temp dir\\n- `~/.openclaw/media/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/agents/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/workspace/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/sandboxes/`\\n- Agent workspace (e.g. `~/clawd/`)\\n\\n`~/Library/Messages/Attachments` is not in any of these.\\n\\nThe iMessage channel has its own separate `attachmentRoots` config (default: `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`) that correctly validates inbound attachments — but those roots are **not passed through** to the image tool's `localRoots` parameter. The two security checks are disconnected.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure iMessage channel with `includeAttachments: true`\\n2. Send an image via iMessage\\n3. Call the `image` tool with the path from the inbound message metadata\\n4. → `LocalMediaAccessError: path-not-allowed`\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\nThe iMessage channel's `attachmentRoots` should be merged into `mediaLocalRoots` when dispatching to the agent, so the `image` tool can read inbound attachments from their native Messages paths. This worked before 2026.3.2.\\n\\n## Config\\n\\n```json\\nchannels.imessage.includeAttachments: true\\n```\\nNo explicit `attachmentRoots` set (using default `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`).\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\nIn the iMessage inbound dispatch path, merge `attachmentRoots` into the `mediaLocalRoots` passed to the tool execution context — similar to how other channels handle scoped media roots from `getAgentScopedMediaLocalRoots`, which only includes:\\n- System temp dir\\n- `~/.openclaw/media/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/agents/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/workspace/`\\n- `~/.openclaw/sandboxes/`\\n- `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`) that correctly validates inbound attachments — but those roots are **not passed through** to the image tool's `localRoots` parameter. The two security checks are disconnected.\\n\\n## Steps to Reproduce\\n\\n1. Configure iMessage channel with `includeAttachments: true`\\n2. Send an image via iMessage\\n3. Call the `image` tool with the path from the inbound message metadata\\n4. → `LocalMediaAccessError: path-not-allowed`\\n\\n## Expected Behavior\\n\\nThe iMessage channel's `attachmentRoots` should be merged into `mediaLocalRoots` when dispatching to the agent, so the `image` tool can read inbound attachments from their native Messages paths. `/Users/*/Library/Messages/Attachments`).\\n\\n## Suggested Fix\\n\\nIn the iMessage inbound dispatch path, merge `attachmentRoots` into the `mediaLocalRoots` passed to the tool execution context — similar to how other channels handle scoped media There is no configuration path to opt into private network access, even in explicitly local gateway deployments where SSRF risk is not a concern.\\n\\n### Proposed solution\\n\\nIntroduce an `allowPrivateNetwork` boolean option for `web_fetch`, `web_search`, and `image_tool`. When running in `local` gateway mode, automatically set `allowPrivateNetwork: true` for a seamless local-first experience. Wire this flag through the SSRF guard (`fetchWithSsrFGuard`) so that private addresses are reachable when the option is enabled.\\n\\n### Alternatives considered\\n\\nManually whitelisting specific IPs in the SSRF guard — too brittle and requires code changes per deployment. Routing local services through a public proxy — adds unnecessary latency and defeats the purpose of self-hosting.\\n\\n### Impact\\n\\n- **Affected:** Teams running self-hosted search engines (SearXNG, etc.) or air-gapped/private deployments\\n- **Severity:** Blocks workflow — private network access is completely unavailable today\\n- **Frequency:** Always, for any private-network deployment\\n- **Consequence:** Self-hosted search is non-functional; operators must use cloud search providers even when a local alternative exists\\n\\n### Evidence/examples\\n\\n- SearXNG Docker setup requires access to `127.x.x.x` or `192.168.x.x` by default\\n- Comparable `allowPrivateNetwork` patterns exist in Fetch API specs and other gateway frameworks\\n- Schema validation for the new flag is covered in `src/config/zod-schema.agent-runtime.ts`\\n- New search providers (Tavily, SearXNG) added alongside this change\\n\\n### Additional information\\n\\n- Must remain backward-compatible: `allowPrivateNetwork` defaults to `false`, preserving existing SSRF protection for all non-local deployments\\n- A troubleshooting guide for plaintext WebSocket/HTTP issues on {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XFRov4sVSVPJUW4N6SXhkV","type":"tool_result","content":[{"type":"text","text":"{\"total_count\":36,\"incomplete_results\":false,\"items\":[{\"id\":4124151632,\"number\":53207,\"state\":\"closed\",\"state_reason\":\"completed\",\"locked\":false,\"title\":\"Auth/OpenAI: fresh token save can revert to stale expired profile under live gateway\",\"body\":\"## Bug\\n\\nSaving a fresh OpenAI token through Configure or Onboard can appear to work, then revert back to a stale expired token while the gateway is still running.\\n\\nRelated: #45516\\n\\n## Root Cause\\n\\nLocked auth-profile writes in `src/agents/auth-profiles/store.ts` reload from `ensureAuthProfileStore(...)`, which prefers the runtime auth-store snapshot when one exists. That snapshot can be stale relative to disk.\\n\\nThis means a normal gateway-side auth write like usage/cooldown/last-good persistence can do this:\\n\\n1. CLI / Configure / Onboard writes a fresh credential to `auth-profiles.json`\\n2. gateway later acquires the auth-store file lock\\n3. locked write reloads the stale in-memory runtime snapshot instead of disk\\n4. gateway saves that stale snapshot back to disk\\n5. fresh token/order/config appears to \\\"revert\\\"\\n\\nThis is the same class of bug as #45516, but it also affects actual credential replacement instead of only auth order.\\n\\n## Repro shape\\n\\n- Have a running gateway with an old OpenAI token loaded in memory\\n- Save a fresh OpenAI token via Configure / Onboard\\n- Trigger CLI / Configure / Onboard writes a fresh credential to `auth-profiles.json`\\n2. gateway later acquires the auth-store file lock\\n3. locked write reloads the stale in-memory runtime snapshot instead of disk\\n4. gateway saves that stale snapshot back to disk\\n5. fresh token/order/config appears to \\\"revert\\\"\\n\\nThis is the same class of bug as #45516, but it also affects actual credential replacement instead of only auth order.\\n\\n## Repro shape\\n\\n- Have a running gateway with an old OpenAI token loaded in memory\\n- Save a fresh OpenAI token via Configure / Onboard\\n- Trigger
